The user is asking about increasing the EC2 EBS volume size. They want to know if they need to disconnect from the instance. No, they don't need to disconnect or stop the instance to resize an EBS volume. AWS allows you to modify EBS volumes while they're attached and in use. The process is: 1. Go to AWS Console ‚Üí EC2 ‚Üí Volumes 2. Select the volume ‚Üí Actions ‚Üí Modify Volume 3. Increase the size 4. Wait for the modification to complete (state goes from "modifying" to "optimizing" to "completed"
Response 04:49:14 ‚Ä¢ 33.95s
Nope! You can resize EBS volumes while the instance is running and you're connected. No downtime needed. **Steps:** 1. **AWS Console** ‚Üí EC2 ‚Üí Volumes 2. Select your volume ‚Üí **Actions** ‚Üí **Modify Volume** 3. Increase the size (e.g., 11GB ‚Üí 30GB) 4. --- summary: "Skills: managed vs workspace, gating rules, and config/env wiring" read_when: - Adding or modifying skills - Changing skill gating or load rules --- # Skills (OpenClaw) OpenClaw uses **[AgentSkills](https://agentskills.io)-compatible** skill folders to teach the agent how to use tools. Each skill is a directory containing a `SKILL.md` with YAML frontmatter and instructions. OpenClaw loads **bundled skills** plus optional local overrides, and filters them at load time based on environment, config, and binary presence. ## Locations and precedence Skills are loaded from **three** places: 1. **Bundled skills**: shipped with the install (npm package or OpenClaw.app) 2. **Managed/local skills**: `~/.openclaw/skills` 3. **Workspace skills**: `<workspace>/skills` If a skill name conflicts, precedence is: `<workspace>/skills` (highest) ‚Üí `~/.openclaw/skills` ‚Üí bundled skills (lowest) Additionally, you can configure extra skill folders (lowest precedence) via `skills.lo

--- summary: "Sub-agents: spawning isolated agent runs that announce results back to the requester chat" read_when: - You want background/parallel work via the agent - You are changing sessions_spawn or sub-agent tool policy --- # Sub-agents Sub-agents are background agent runs spawned from an existing agent run. They run in their own session (`agent:<agentId>:subagent:<uuid>`) and, when finished, **announce** their result back to the requester chat channel. ## Slash command Use `/subagents` to inspect or control sub-agent runs for the **current session**: - `/subagents list` - `/subagents stop <id|#|all>` - `/subagents log <id|#> [limit] [tools]` - `/subagents info <id|#>` - `/subagents send <id|#> <message>` `/subagents info` shows run metadata (status, timestamps, session id, transcript path, cleanup). Primary goals: - Parallelize ‚Äúresearch / long task / slow tool‚Äù work without blocking the main run. - Keep sub-agents isolated by default (session separation + optional sa

--- summary: "Multi-agent routing: isolated agents, channel accounts, and bindings" title: Multi-Agent Routing read_when: "You want multiple isolated agents (workspaces + auth) in one gateway process." status: active --- # Multi-Agent Routing Goal: multiple _isolated_ agents (separate workspace + `agentDir` + sessions), plus multiple channel accounts (e.g. two WhatsApps) in one running Gateway. Inbound is routed to an agent via bindings. ## What is ‚Äúone agent‚Äù? An **agent** is a fully scoped brain with its own: - **Workspace** (files, AGENTS.md/SOUL.md/USER.md, local notes, persona rules). - **State directory** (`agentDir`) for auth profiles, model registry, and per-agent config. - **Session store** (chat history + routing state) under `~/.openclaw/agents/<agentId>/sessions`. Auth profiles are **per-agent**. Each agent reads from its own: ``` ~/.openclaw/agents/<agentId>/agent/auth-profiles.json ``` Main agent credentials are **not** shared automatically. Cron is the Gateway‚Äôs built-in scheduler. It persists jobs, wakes the agent at the right time, and can optionally deliver output back to a chat. If you want _‚Äúrun this every morning‚Äù_ or _‚Äúpoke the agent in 20 minutes‚Äù_, cron is the mechanism. ## TL;DR - Cron runs **inside the Gateway** (not inside the model). - Jobs persist under `~/.openclaw/cron/` so restarts don‚Äôt lose schedules. - Two execution styles: - **Main session**: enqueue a system event, then run on the next heartbeat. - **Isolated**: run a dedicated agent turn in `cron:<jobId>`, optionally deliver output. - Wakeups are first-cla

# Creating Custom Skills üõ† OpenClaw is designed to be easily extensible. "Skills" are the primary way to add new capabilities to your assistant. ## What is a Skill? A skill is a directory containing a `SKILL.md` file (which provides instructions and tool definitions to the LLM) and optionally some scripts or resources. ## Step-by-Step: Your First Skill ### 1. Create the Directory Skills live in your workspace, usually `~/.openclaw/workspace/skills/`. Create a new folder for your skill: ```bash mkdir -p ~/.openclaw/workspace/skills/hello-world ``` ### 2. Define the `SKILL.md` Create a `SKILL.md` file in that directory. This file uses YAML frontmatter for metadata and Markdown for instructions. ```markdown --- name: hello_world description: A simple skill that says hello. --- # Hello World Skill When the user asks for a greeting, use the `echo` tool to say "Hello from your custom skill!". ``` ### 3. Add Tools (Optional) You can define custom tools in the frontmatter or inst

OpenClaw is an open-source gateway that connects messaging platforms (WhatsApp, Telegram, Discord, iMessage) to AI coding agents, letting you interact with agents directly from your phone. It runs a single Gateway process that bridges chat channels to Pi agents via RPC, supports multi-agent routing, streaming responses, media handling, and includes browser/mobile control UIs. The system defaults to loopback-only WebSocket connections for security, with optional remote access via SSH tunnel or Tailscale. Installation requires Node ‚â•22 and uses a guided wizard (`openclaw onboard`) that sets up platform services (launchd/systemd), after which you pair WhatsApp Web via QR code and send messages through the gateway to get agent responses with full tool streaming and per-sender session isolation. 8.7s ¬∑ $0.0112 ¬∑ 1.1k words ¬∑ anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-5 ¬∑ ‚Üë2.8k ‚Üì176 Œî3.0k

{'path': '/home/ubuntu/clawd/scripts/analyze_session.py', 'content': '\nimport json\nimport glob\nimport os\nfrom datetime import datetime\n\ndef parse_session(file_path):\n events = []\n with open(file_path, \'r\') as f:\n for line in f:\n try:\n entry = json.loads(line)\n timestamp = entry.get(\'timestamp\')\n if not timestamp: continue\n \n # Normalize timestamp (handle Z or numeric)\n if isinstance(timestamp, (int, float)):\n dt = datetime.fromtimestamp(timestamp/1000.0) # Assume ms if number\n else:\n dt = datetime.fromisoformat(timestamp.replace(\'Z\', \'+00:00\'))\n \n msg = entry.get(\'message\', {})\n role = msg.get(\'role\')\n content = msg.get(\'content\', [])\n \n # Extract interesting events\n if role == \'user\':\n events.append({\'type\': \'user_msg\', \'time\': dt, \'summary\': \'User Input\'})\n \n elif role == \'assistant\':\n # Look for thinking and tool calls\n if isinstance(content, list):\n for part in content:\n if part.get(\'type\') == \'thinking\':\n events.append({\'type\': \'thinking\', \'time\': dt, \'summary\': \'Thinking...\'})\n elif part.get(\'type\') == \'toolCall\':\n tool_name = part.get(\'name\')\n events.append({\'type\': \'tool_call\', \'time\': dt, \'tool\': tool_name, \'summary\': f\'Call: {tool_name}\'})\n elif part.get(\'type\') == \'text\':\n # Text output often comes with tools or thinking, check if meaningful\n text = part.get(\'text\', \'\').strip()\n if text:\n events.append({\'type\': \'response\', \'time\': dt, \'summary\': \'Response\'})\n \n elif role == \'toolResult\':\n tool_name = msg.get(\'toolName\')\n is_error = msg.get(\'isError\', False)\n status = "Error" if is_error else "Success"\n events.append({\'type\': \'tool_result\', \'time\': dt, \'tool\': tool_name, \'summary\': f\'Result: {tool_name} ({status})\'})\n \n except Exception as e:\n continue\n \n return events\n\ndef analyze_timings(events):\n if not events: return []\n \n timeline = []\n start_time = events[0][\'time\']\n \n for i in range(len(events) - 1):\n current = events[i]\n next_event = events[i+1]\n duration = (next_event[\'time\'] - current[\'time\']).total_seconds()\n \n item = {\n \'event\': current[\'summary\'],\n \'type\': current[\'type\'],\n \'start\': (current[\'time\'] - start_time).total_seconds(),\n \'duration\': duration,\n \'tool\': current.get(\'tool\')\n }\n timeline.append(item)\n \n return timeline\n\n# Find latest session\nsession_files = glob.glob(os.path.expanduser(\'~/.openclaw/agents/main/sessions/*.jsonl\'))\nlatest_session = max(session_files, key=os.path.getmtime)\n\nprint(f"Analyzing {latest_session}...")\nevents = parse_session(latest_session)\ntimeline = analyze_timings(events)\n\nfor item in timeline:\n print(f"{item[\'start\']:.1f}s | {item[\'duration\']:.1f}s | {item[\'event\']}")\n'}
